<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1289984135">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289984135" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21081005-antonio" class="left imgcol" title="Antonio"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446948833p2/21081005.jpg" alt="Antonio" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1289984135?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21081005-antonio" class="user" title="Antonio">Antonio</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/597030.La_luz_fant_stica" title="Paperback 9788497931786" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21081005-antonio?shelf=sagas" class="actionLinkLite">sagas</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21081005-antonio?shelf=electr%C3%B3nicos" class="actionLinkLite">electrónicos</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21081005-antonio?shelf=fantas%C3%ADa" class="actionLinkLite">fantasía</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1289984135">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3974452767417267507">Decidí darle una segunda oportunidad al Mundodisco, porque los fans de Pratchett me han comentado que la saga lo merece, no porque tenga algún problema obsesivo compulsivo con dejar cosas sin terminar...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433093974ra/15048937.gif" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433056625ra/15044408.gif" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433057032ra/15044472.gif" /><br /><br />y ¡Wau! las diferencias entre <em>El color de la magia</em> y <em>La luz fantástica</em> son <u>abismales</u>, casi todos los problemas que tuve con el primer libro se resuelven acá, <strong>este si me pareció gracioso, si es concluyente y...</strong> resuelve una incógnita del primer libro que me molestaba bastante <strong>Rincewind</strong>, a pesar de</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3974452767417267507">Decidí darle una segunda oportunidad al Mundodisco, porque los fans de Pratchett me han comentado que la saga lo merece, no porque tenga algún problema obsesivo compulsivo con dejar cosas sin terminar...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433093974ra/15048937.gif" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433056625ra/15044408.gif" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433057032ra/15044472.gif" /><br /><br />y ¡Wau! las diferencias entre <em>El color de la magia</em> y <em>La luz fantástica</em> son <u>abismales</u>, casi todos los problemas que tuve con el primer libro se resuelven acá, <strong>este si me pareció gracioso, si es concluyente y...</strong> resuelve una incógnita del primer libro que me molestaba bastante <strong>Rincewind</strong>, a pesar de ser un mago bastante simplón y no hacer magia, sobrevive a toda la serie de eventos desafortunados que se le ha presentado, <u>
  <strong>pues hay una razón para ello.</strong>
</u> <br /><br />En la luz fantástica continuaremos la historia de <strong>Rincewind y Dosflores</strong> (Two-flo-wers) <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433093235i/15048828.jpg" /><br /><br />esta pareja dispareja que ha desarrollado una especie de amistad gracias a todas sus aventuras y cuya travesía por el Disco aun no termina, y que seria de ellos sin el fiel <strong>Equipaje</strong> el mejor de los artilugios mágicos de todos los tiempos, ademas, esta vez conoceremos a <strong>Cohen el bárbaro</strong>, el guerrero mas famoso del disco, que ya tiene 87 años y esta sufriendo problemas de espalda, lo que no le impide realizar proezas, solo las hace mas graciosas.<br /><br /><strong>En fin, esta libro me gusto mucho, me saco varias risas y me dejo con ganas de leer mas del Mundodisco</strong>, me alegra haberle dado otra oportunidad a la saga, y creo que <u>si habéis leído El color de la magia, debes leer este libro</u>, quien sabe quizás quedes <blockquote>
  <em>sonriendo como un necrófilo en un depósito de cadáveres.</em>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3974452767417267507">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1384357085">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384357085" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words" class="left imgcol" title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443086847p2/38658747.jpg" alt="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1384357085?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 14, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words" class="user" title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)">Evelyn (devours and digests words)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11186726-the-light-fantastic" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=great-characterization" class="actionLinkLite">great-characterization</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=unique-story-lines" class="actionLinkLite">unique-story-lines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=mind-fucked" class="actionLinkLite">mind-fucked</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=in-love-with-the-guys" class="actionLinkLite">in-love-with-the-guys</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=worldbuilding-for-the-win" class="actionLinkLite">worldbuilding-for-the-win</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=fantastical" class="actionLinkLite">fantastical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=cover-porn" class="actionLinkLite">cover-porn</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=fey-folks" class="actionLinkLite">fey-folks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=series-i-actually-like" class="actionLinkLite">series-i-actually-like</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=messed-with-my-feelings" class="actionLinkLite">messed-with-my-feelings</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=writing-i-would-love-to-imitate" class="actionLinkLite">writing-i-would-love-to-imitate</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=bagful-of-laughs" class="actionLinkLite">bagful-of-laughs</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=a-touch-of-satire" class="actionLinkLite">a-touch-of-satire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1384357085">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6964889431561159307"><em>"Inside every sane person, there's a madman struggling to get out. That's what I've always thought. No one goes mad quicker than a totally sane person." </em><br /><br /><strong>The second installment in the Discworld series is a bigger, funnier delight. One heck of a Laugh Out Loud read.</strong><br /><br />Something I consider very special in Sir Terry Pratchett's works is that many authors can pull off a joke every once in a while in their stories but <strong>Mr Pratchett managed to keep the whole thing comical, while at the time <em>satirical.</em></strong> Not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6964889431561159307"><em>"Inside every sane person, there's a madman struggling to get out. That's what I've always thought. No one goes mad quicker than a totally sane person." </em><br /><br /><strong>The second installment in the Discworld series is a bigger, funnier delight. One heck of a Laugh Out Loud read.</strong><br /><br />Something I consider very special in Sir Terry Pratchett's works is that many authors can pull off a joke every once in a while in their stories but <strong>Mr Pratchett managed to keep the whole thing comical, while at the time <em>satirical.</em></strong> Not once did I not grin or snort out loud.<br /><br />In <a title="The Colour of Magic The Illustrated Screenplay by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833512.The_Colour_of_Magic_The_Illustrated_Screenplay"> The Colour of Magic</a>, Rincewind was last seen (read?) falling off the rim of the world. Well, he landed safely on his arse. Thank goodness or he couldn't be much use if he's dead.<br /><br />Things are turning quite grim now. Great A'Tuin the turtle is wading its giant flippers toward a 'red star'. The closer it is (I feel very sorry for calling the World Turtle an 'it' but in my defense, 'it's' sex is still undetermined afterall!) to the star, the weaker and more unbalanced the magic is back in Discworld!<br /><br />The only way to prevent the apocalypse is to recite all 8 spells from a magic book called Octavo. However one last spell is missing. Where could it be?! It also didn't help Rincewind's situation and mood when he found out that there's a certain prophecy about him.<br /><br />I'm not a big reader when it comes to books with apocalypse in it looming just around the corner. Too bleak, I say. But this was a purely fun ride that follows with Rincewind's unfortunate adventures.<br /><br />The worldbuilding is still just as bizarre as the last book. Except now it has a fairytale feel to it. There's even a scene where Rincewind and Twoflower took refuge in a gingerbread house! Sounds familiar? *cough* Hansel and Gretel! *cough*<br /><br /><strong>Characterizations [humans, fantastical creatures and things alike]: </strong><br /><br />I have a very special place in my heart for nearly all the people <s>and creatures</s> in the book. Of course I have certain favourites myself but I couldn't resist liking nearly everything and everyone. It sounds so corny of me, I know. But damn it, I can't help myself not when they're all so fleshed out well. Definitely not when they each have their own unique quirky personality.<br /><br />Rincewind shows even more of his cynicism and it didn't exactly help his ill bedside manners being partnered with the impossibly, insufferably optimistic Twoflower.<br /><blockquote>
<br />"I expect everything will turn out quite all right in the end," said Twoflower.<br /><br />Rincewind looked at him. Remarks like that always threw him off.<br /><br />"Do you really believe that? I mean," he said. "Really?"<br /><br />"Well, things generally do work out satisfactorily, when you come to think about it."<br /><br />"If you think the total disruption of my life in the last year is satisfactory then you might be right. I've lost count of the times I've nearly been killed--"<br /><br />"Twenty-seven," said Twoflower.<br /><br /><em>"What?"</em> </blockquote><br /><br />He held a great disdain within him toward people and situations in life. He's not just <strong>cynical</strong>, I like to think of him as <strong>pessimistic</strong> too. He also has a knack of running in the opposite directions from things he's terrified of instead of plunging straight into the fire and save the day. Some people would say that he's quite the <strong>coward</strong>. I would say that he's quite the <strong>survivalist.</strong><br /><br /><blockquote>'He always held that panic was the best means of survival; back in the olden days, his theory went, people faced with hungry saber-toothed tigers could be divided very simply into those who panicked and those who stood there saying. "What a magnificent brute!" and "Here, pussy." </blockquote><br /><br />Rincewind's snappy moods, impatience and crankiness have really grown on me. Irregardless of how distasteful his actions may be at times!<br /><br />I have to tip my hat on behalf of Twoflower, the first tourist of Ankh-Morpork may be the only one who can understand and tolerate Rincewind. While he is pessimistic, <strong>Twoflower is optimistic.</strong> Rincewind's cowardly but Twoflowers's <strong>noble and is willing to sacrifice himself to save others.</strong> Rincewind is quick to rage but Twoflower's best merits are his patience and his forgiving nature.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Against the whole of human experience Twoflower believed that if only people would talk to each other, have a few drinks, exchange pictures of their grandchildren, maybe take in a show or something, then everything could be sorted out. He also believed that people were basically good but sometimes had their bad days."</blockquote><br /><br />How can I not resist someone like him? I can't!<strong> He's so good-hearted, it either made you despise how he's so insufferably annoying at that or... you find him irresistible.</strong> It is the latter for me.<br /><br />Then there's<strong> The Luggage</strong>, it's name suggest<em> what</em> it is. A luggage that carries laundries for its master! Except it's no ordinary luggage. For one thing, it has hundreds of tiny little legs to take it anywhere. It's lid serves as a mouth and when it wants to look menancing, it snaps the lid up and down. <strong>Don't get too close - it's a luggage that bites and snaps <s>and eats people up!</s></strong><br /><br />With the Luggage in your possession, you can be in no harm as long as:<br /><br /><blockquote>a) you're not trying to harm it's master and his friends.<br />b) you don't kick its wooden sides and be a big bully.<br />c) you don't try to force open its lid apart to see what treasure is inside (there are usually none).</blockquote><br /><br />So aside from looking menancing, what else does it do? You'd be awed that not only The Luggage is useful in carrying loads,<strong> it is also very loyal, quick in thinking and even quicker so in taking actions</strong> (with those hundreds of little legs? No doubt)<strong> to save those in distress</strong>. Don't ask me how a luggage can think. I have no idea! Point is, the Luggage can be real scary to the point that even barbarians soil their trousers. You should be scared.<br /><br />Then there are the minor people, creatures and things alike such as a group of incompetent swordsmen led by a woman, talking trees, a goblin, an imp who paints, a barbarian, DEATH and his comrades, stone trolls, a cursed shopkeeper, a mob of crazy superstitious people with pitchforks.... and so on and so forth. I expected to get clogged up with all these many minor characters coming and going. But not-so-surprisingly, I didn't feel confused or got side tracked by them. Each one of them has personalities and they're not forgettable. Not when they do or say something incredibly incredible, funny or stupid.<strong> Pratchett can write about the smallest pebble on a ground of dirt and still make it interesting and full of persona.</strong><br /><br />As a final conclusion, I can't say much except that... well, <strong>this book</strong> was just fucking fantastic and it <strong>won my heart and soul completely</strong>. That about sums up my thoughts. <br /><br />Besides, it's almost impossible to pick apart or find anything wrong in something that can switch on your 'HAHA' button each seconds. <em>The jokes are distracting!</em><br /><br /><strong>
  <u>Doctor's Prescription and Warning:</u>
</strong><br /><br />This is the medicine for when you feel blue or angry.<br /><br />No, it's not supposed to be some pills.<br /><br />It's<em> this</em> book.<br /><br />However, read with care for each sentences and every passages are induced with high dosages of humour. Limit your level of intake in case you overdosed on the words and choke on your spit bellowing with laughter.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6964889431561159307">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_28987832">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28987832" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1385106-jamie" class="left imgcol" title="Jamie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1217535570p2/1385106.jpg" alt="Jamie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/28987832?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 01, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1385106-jamie" class="user" title="Jamie">Jamie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer28987832">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10236951246820858772">I'm pretty sure people have told me about Pratchett and his Diskworld series before, usually working in the phrase "He's the Douglas Adams of fantasy" into the description. But the problem was that I always felt that I had had enough of Adams after the third Hithiker's Guide to the Galaxy book, and whenever I scanned Pratchett's section in the bookstore I was immediately put off by not knowing where to start reading among the approximately five hundred thousand Diskworld books. I'm glad I finall</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10236951246820858772">I'm pretty sure people have told me about Pratchett and his Diskworld series before, usually working in the phrase "He's the Douglas Adams of fantasy" into the description. But the problem was that I always felt that I had had enough of Adams after the third Hithiker's Guide to the Galaxy book, and whenever I scanned Pratchett's section in the bookstore I was immediately put off by not knowing where to start reading among the approximately five hundred thousand Diskworld books. I'm glad I finally took the time to find out that these two books, The Colour of Magic and The Light Fantastic, jointly comprise the first tale in the series, and that they were definitely worth reading.<br /><br />The Diskworld books are essentially satire of the high fantasy genre, or at least that's the foundation upon which everything else is built. This pair of books follows the misadventures of Rincewind, a utterly inept and thoroughly cowardly wizard, and Twoflowers, a clueless traveler who happens to be in possession of both endless optimism and a magical suitcase that's always wandering off and messily devouring people who get in its way. Things go from bad to worse for the two as divine powers both deliver them into and yank them out of all kinds of fantastic perils.<br /><br />As someone who grew up reading plenty of this kind of thing and playing a lot of Dungeons&amp; Dragons, I'm familiar enough with the genre and trappings that Pratchett lampoons. Yes, there's the Conan parody, there's the Dragonriders of Pern tribute, there's the in-joke about Leiber's Fafhrd and Gray Mouser. But that's easy. The thing that made me almost immediately fall in love with these books is the author's dry wit and his ability to derive humor not only from the absurdity of the story (and believe me, it gets plenty absurd) but also from just good old fashioned turns of phrase, wry commentary, and jokes. The guy just has an amazing ability to stuff five or six jokes into a single sentence, most of them making masterful use of that trusty standby of British humor, irony. It's really smart and really funny, and the fact that it builds on the inherent silliness of the high fantasy genre is just icing.<br /><br />I should also note how imaginative Pratchett is, which is a useful quality given his subject matter. He bounces his heroes from one (generally horrible and dangerous) situation to another at a frantic pace, and his ability to come up with new material and new situations amazes me. And while many of them are obvious parodies of fantasy staples, just as many seem to be wholly new creations. As one small (and obligatory) example, the Diskworld itself is a flat coin of a world that rides atop four enormous elephants, who themselves ride on the back of a colossal turtle with two continent-sized flippers that it uses to swim slowly through the cold reaches of space.<br /><br />But at the same time, if I have one complaint about these first two books, it's that they're almost maniacal in their plotting. While it's nice to see Pratchett's considerable imagination and humor on display as we go from situation to situation, the first book reads like an extended doodle with little plot and a whole "gods playing games with mortals" subtext that's entirely dropped in the next book. There's also one Conan the Barbarian parody that's abruptly dropped in favor of another Conan the Barbarian parody who Pratchett apparently liked better. It's not until the latter part of the second book does an overall plot come into play, but honestly I was enjoying myself so much I really didn't mind. Expect to see lots more Discworld books reviewed here in the future. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10236951246820858772">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer928714938">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2750279434724910113">This book was every bit as fun as the last- maybe more so. Since this is number two in series order, I am getting a feel for where the author was at the point in time it was written. The character development seems more vivid. Rincewind, the Luggage, the Druid sacrifice girl, and the over the hill barbarian fighter are characters that will live with me long after this series is done.<br />This story has more of a quest feel to it than the last one did. It definitely builds to a strong climax. In order</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2750279434724910113">This book was every bit as fun as the last- maybe more so. Since this is number two in series order, I am getting a feel for where the author was at the point in time it was written. The character development seems more vivid. Rincewind, the Luggage, the Druid sacrifice girl, and the over the hill barbarian fighter are characters that will live with me long after this series is done.<br />This story has more of a quest feel to it than the last one did. It definitely builds to a strong climax. In order to avert certain doom, all of the eight great spells must be read in order. The eighth and final spell is, of course, in Rincewind’s mind. His death would solve that problem for the planet’s most powerful spell casters. <br /> The story progresses through one mishap after another as the author continues to add characters and build his world. Rather than read these books by order of character type (for example, all of the Rincewind stories followed by all of the Witches stories and so forth), I have chosen to attempt to read them chronologically. I think it gives a clear picture of where the author is at in a point in time and what his conception of this world and these characters is and is becoming.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2750279434724910113">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_963753962">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/963753962" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10743961-rob" class="left imgcol" title="Rob"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" alt="Rob" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/963753962?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10743961-rob" class="user" title="Rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6457620-the-light-fantastic" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=discworld" class="actionLinkLite">discworld</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer963753962">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16398734360267009415"><strong>Executive Summary:</strong> I enjoyed this one a lot more than <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_">The Color of Magic</a>, and it made me glad I read that book first rather than starting with one of the later in the series.<br /><br /><strong> <u>Full Review</u> </strong><br />A moment of silence for the passing of a great man.<br /><br /><br /><br />It's a shame it took the passing of Terry Pratchett for me to give this series a second chance. I've had numerous people tell me how much I'd like it. It was recommended again to me when I said I was in a funk and wanted something light and fun just a few days b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16398734360267009415"><strong>Executive Summary:</strong> I enjoyed this one a lot more than <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_">The Color of Magic</a>, and it made me glad I read that book first rather than starting with one of the later in the series.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</strong><br />A moment of silence for the passing of a great man.<br /><br /><br /><br />It's a shame it took the passing of Terry Pratchett for me to give this series a second chance. I've had numerous people tell me how much I'd like it. It was recommended again to me when I said I was in a funk and wanted something light and fun just a few days before his passing. <br /><br />I just wasn't sure about it though. I'm often stubborn. I know it. I like to read things in publication order. I know this series is more like a loose collection of stories set in the same world, but I still want to read it in the order it came out. So I read <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_">The Color of Magic</a> last year, and it was alright.<br /><br />I did plan on reading this book at some point, but I kept putting it off. I wish I hadn't. The humor was better, the plot was more interesting, and some great new characters were introduced.<br /><br />And the puns. Man there are some great puns in here. I had to stop reading for a few minutes because I was laughing so hard. I'm not normally big on puns, but they really worked for me in this book. I won't ruin them for you though, you should read them for yourself.<br /><br />So now I'm hooked on the series. I jumped right into <a title="Equal Rites (Discworld, #3; Witches #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34507.Equal_Rites__Discworld___3__Witches__1_">Equal Rites</a> and I'm nearly done with that. I'll likely be jumping right into <a title="Mort (Discworld, #4; Death, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386372.Mort__Discworld___4__Death___1_">Mort</a> after that.<br /><br />I'm sad Mr. Pratchett has left us, and that I didn't get a chance to meet him and thank him for his great work. But I'm excited by the fact that I have nearly 40 more books to enjoy. I may have to pace myself though as there will sadly only be one more to come.<br /><br />I can't say you should be stubborn like I am, and read in publication order. Most people seem to recommend starting with <a title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_">Guards! Guards!</a> or <a title="Small Gods (Discworld, #13) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34484.Small_Gods__Discworld___13_">Small Gods</a>. I will say that if you do start with <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_">The Color of Magic</a> make sure you read this one too, because not only is it a continuation of the plot, it's a vast improvement in every way.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16398734360267009415">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1313218222">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10884655879022586464">Sería un 3,75 o cerca del 4, no lo tengo del todo claro.<br />Esta es la continuación de El color de la magia, el primer volumen de la saga Mundodisco, siendo la única novela de la saga que continua directamente con los sucesos del libro anterior.<br />En este libro, tras salvarse de caer por el borde del mundo; Dosflores, Rincewind y el querido equipaje vuelven a meterse en muchos más líos. Una estrella roja amenaza la vida de la gran tortuga ATuin, y la Universidad Invisible (la de los magos) está tratand</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10884655879022586464">Sería un 3,75 o cerca del 4, no lo tengo del todo claro.<br />Esta es la continuación de El color de la magia, el primer volumen de la saga Mundodisco, siendo la única novela de la saga que continua directamente con los sucesos del libro anterior.<br />En este libro, tras salvarse de caer por el borde del mundo; Dosflores, Rincewind y el querido equipaje vuelven a meterse en muchos más líos. Una estrella roja amenaza la vida de la gran tortuga A´Tuin, y la Universidad Invisible (la de los magos) está tratando de reunir los 8 hechizos del Octavo, una hechizos prohibidos de gran poder que creen que podrán salvar el mundo. Uno de ellos como sabemos desde el primer libro lo tiene Rincewind en su cabeza, por ello, junto a un guerrero legendario del disco llamado Cohen y una virgen que iba a ser sacrificada por druidas llamada Bethan; trataran de lidiar con los viejos profesores de la Universidad Invisible.<br />Al igual que en la primera parte, me lo he pasado muy bien, o incluso mejor, dado que el libro tiene mayor coherencia narrativa y ya estamos acostumbrados al mundo. El estilo es el mismo, con un humor absurdo y delirante, con algunos diálogos desternillantes y con unos personajes geniales. De nuevo la historia es totalmente absurda y está llena de guiños a otros clásicos, como Conan o Hanzel y Gretel. Los personajes vuelven a ser algo maravilloso y desternillante; y también os encontraréis en esta ocasión con árboles parlantes, casas de chocolate, trolls amigables, guerreros legendarios y magia, mucha magia. Eso si, tengo claro que me ha gustado mucho más que el primero, es menos caótico y más fácil de seguir la trama; y la enseñanza de que casi nada es lo que puede parecer es una de las reflexiones más adecuadas. Lo que me ha fastidiado un poquito es el final abierto, y la perdida de ese personaje que me gustaba tanto, pero creo que reaparece en alguna nueva aventura.<br />Tengo muchas ganas de continuar con la saga, poquito a poco pero con paso firme, pero de momento me esta gustando el reto de leerlas en orden de publicación.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10884655879022586464">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1106150664">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106150664" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="left imgcol" title="Lyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428721461p2/5253785.jpg" alt="Lyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1106150664?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="user" title="Lyn">Lyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1106150664">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10422930832114510537">Reading Sir Terry Pratchett’s Discworld series makes me smile.<br /><br />Three years after Terry Pratchett published <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Color of Magic</a>, the first Discworld book, he published the second, The Light Fantastic, having decided convincingly that this was a worthwhile project.<br /><br />Though the action in The Light Fantastic takes over immediately following the events in the first book, Rincewind has fallen off of the edge of the world, this novel seems to gather momentum from a good but somewhat shaky start and proceed</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10422930832114510537">Reading Sir Terry Pratchett’s Discworld series makes me smile.<br /><br />Three years after Terry Pratchett published <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Color of Magic</a>, the first Discworld book, he published the second, The Light Fantastic, having decided convincingly that this was a worthwhile project.<br /><br />Though the action in The Light Fantastic takes over immediately following the events in the first book, Rincewind has fallen off of the edge of the world, this novel seems to gather momentum from a good but somewhat shaky start and proceed with a comic authority. While The Colour of Magic could have been a funny stand alone, Pratchett’s entry with The Light Fantastic seems to usher in a certainty that the Discworld as a multiverse, as a literary institution, has begun and with no end in sight.<br /><br />Actually, I suppose he could have written a third, making the obligatory trilogy and then moving on to something else, but Pratchett wraps up his story tidily and leaves the fertile soil of Discworld as a fun idea from which more books can be written. (As I write this pithy little review in 2014 there are 40 works in publication, and the series is a phenomenon with over 80 million novels sold and in 37 languages. (Pratchett himself was knighted in 2009).<br /><br />So what is all the fuss about? Our heroes Rincewind and Twoflower go on an adventure to save the world, or try to, or accidentally end up in all the right places, or something. The real hero of the novel, and of the series, is Pratchett himself. It is his narration that amuses, cajoles, and encourages laughter and that keeps the reader’s attention. Playfully, and with wry English humor, Pratchett weaves a fun fantasy story with references to Biblical, classical, and mythical themes as well as modern subjects like Conan the Barbarian.<br /><br />It is simply, a lot of fun.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416530672i/11990851._SX540_.jpg" /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10422930832114510537">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_79886412">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79886412" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin" class="left imgcol" title="Mike (the Paladin)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450193915p2/2187043.jpg" alt="Mike (the Paladin)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/79886412?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 05, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin" class="user" title="Mike (the Paladin)">Mike (the Paladin)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/833461.The_Light_Fantastic" title="Hardcover 9780861402038" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79886412">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3722318320593807113">If you read The Color of Magic, you most probably got this book as the the one preceding it (the aforementioned The Color of Magic) ended with Rincewind falling off the edge of the Discworld.... talk about a "cliff-hanger ending". In this one we'll go from there to what could be the end of the Discworld itself and possibly, well everything else. It all depends on Rincewind....scary thought that.<br /><br />"Synopsisizers" (I believe I just made that word up, so bear with me, please) anyway, "the people who</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3722318320593807113">If you read The Color of Magic, you most probably got this book as the the one preceding it (the aforementioned The Color of Magic) ended with Rincewind falling off the edge of the Discworld.... talk about a "cliff-hanger ending". In this one we'll go from there to what could be the end of the Discworld itself and possibly, well everything else. It all depends on Rincewind....scary thought that.<br /><br />"Synopsisizers" (I believe I just made that word up, so bear with me, please) anyway, "the people who write synopses" love to say books (and for that matter movies, TV programs, songs, poems, and everthing else) are "irreverent". They think this will appeal to the rebel in each of us I suppose. In this case Pratchett's writings do tend to skewer "dogmas" but he does it pretty much across the board getting the irreligious as well as the religious. I'm a Christian and haven't found myself "outraged" to the point of hurling the book across the room or anything. I enjoy Sir Terry's work and while I'd probably disagree with him across the board on spiritual matters, I think I'd like him.<br /><br />I think that most anyone with an open mind (and maybe are sure what they themselves actually believe and realize that this is that arcane "thing" called "humor")can enjoy the Discworld books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3722318320593807113">...more</a>

          </span>

Cohen was pretty spry for his age and I loved his loyalty to the gang.<br /><br />The ending was better in this one but it felt a little anticlimatic to me, didn't feel the tension in some parts even though it was well written. <br /><br />Crappy review but I'm tired :-P haha.. Would recommend, another fun adventure from Mr. Pratchett.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/146424501?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1376766-becky" class="user" title="Becky">Becky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=humorous" class="actionLinkLite">humorous</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional" class="actionLinkLite">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_kindle" class="actionLinkLite">ebook_kindle</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer146424501">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12003180638037433841"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146424481">I didn't really care for The Colour of Magic.</a> So I wasn't sure what to expect from The Light Fantastic, but I figured either it would be more of the same, or slightly better. And thankfully, it was slightly better. There was a plot! (Of sorts.) And a single storyline! (Mostly.) And humor! (I lol'ed once.)<br /><br />All are things that Colour didn't have - at least not in my opinion. But I can't say that I loved Light. I'm thinking that it might just be me, though. I like humor, and I even like bizarre rand</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12003180638037433841"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146424481">I didn't really care for The Colour of Magic.</a> So I wasn't sure what to expect from The Light Fantastic, but I figured either it would be more of the same, or slightly better. And thankfully, it was slightly better. There was a plot! (Of sorts.) And a single storyline! (Mostly.) And humor! (I lol'ed once.)<br /><br />All are things that Colour didn't have - at least not in my opinion. But I can't say that I loved Light. I'm thinking that it might just be me, though. I like humor, and I even like bizarre randomness... to a point. I can't help but feel like this whole world is just centered around silliness for its own sake, and I like my humor to be a little more measured and intentional than that. <br /><br />I found myself laughing at the humor and one-liners in the dialogue, and rolling my eyes at the whimsy of everything else. I just... don't care for that. I need rules and to understand how the world works - and apparently in Discworld, anything and everything is possible. It makes me twitchy. <br /><br />Maybe I'll adjust and adapt to it, because at this point I do intend to continue the series. At least until the twitching starts to affect my health, and then I'll call it quits. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12003180638037433841">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5454475-tfitoby" class="user" title="Tfitoby">Tfitoby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/601239.The_Light_Fantastic" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552128483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5454475-tfitoby?shelf=fantastical" class="actionLinkLite">fantastical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5454475-tfitoby?shelf=funny" class="actionLinkLite">funny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer168812598">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17953839364631503434"><strong>Unseen University but not as you know it.</strong><br /><br />With my awful and dreaded exercise regime continuing so too does my revisit to the early works of the Discworld thanks to the readings of Nigel Planer.<br /><br />Rincewind, last seen falling off of the disc has been saved from certain death once more thanks to spoilers that won't be mentioned and now must save the disc from a fiery death and evil wizards.<br /><br />The problem with going back to these early novels is that things arenlt as you remember them. It's like an altern</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17953839364631503434"><strong>Unseen University but not as you know it.</strong><br /><br />With my awful and dreaded exercise regime continuing so too does my revisit to the early works of the Discworld thanks to the readings of Nigel Planer.<br /><br />Rincewind, last seen falling off of the disc has been saved from certain death once more thanks to spoilers that won't be mentioned and now must save the disc from a fiery death and evil wizards.<br /><br />The problem with going back to these early novels is that things arenlt as you remember them. It's like an alternate universe where everything is the same only slightly different. Ridcully is beyond larger than life in the later novels and the supporting cast of wizards rounder, more interesting, so that this early incarnation of the internal politics of the wizards <strong>feels a bit silly.</strong> The same can be said for the trolls too. They're not the same entities from Thud for example.<br /><br />That aside this is <strong>a jolly good romp</strong> through fantasy cliches and a not so subtle critique of the weaknesses of the masses in the grip of fear. The pairing of Rincewind and Twoflower continue to grow dynamically and the development of the luggage as an actual character is fun to read. Added to the ensemble this time is the legendary hero Cohen The Barbarian and his virgin wife Bethan who provide an extra dimension of fun.<br /><br />Cohen and the trip to the Domain of Death stand out as high points for me and help this second book in the series to <strong>surpass The Colour of Magic in terms of pleasure and entertainment.</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17953839364631503434">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1188462593">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14930825170502562744"><strong> <em> The important thing about having lots of things to remember is that you've got to go somewhere afterwards where you can remember them, you see? You've got to stop. You haven't really been anywhere until you've got back home." </em> </strong><br /><br />The Discworld is a Disc sitting on the backs of four elephants, standing on the shell of a giant turtle that is slowly swimming it's way through Space...<br /><br />And as befits a world so ridiculous, it is filled with an array of equally ridiculous and loveable characters, includi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14930825170502562744"><strong>
  <em> The important thing about having lots of things to remember is that you've got to go somewhere afterwards where you can remember them, you see? You've got to stop. You haven't really been anywhere until you've got back home." </em>
</strong><br /><br />The Discworld is a Disc sitting on the backs of four elephants, standing on the shell of a giant turtle that is slowly swimming it's way through Space...<br /><br />And as befits a world so ridiculous, it is filled with an array of equally ridiculous and loveable characters, including a piece of travelling Luggage with lots of tiny legs and an intimidating appetite. This is one of the most hilariously enjoyable series I've found in a long time.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>"In a distant forest a wolf howled, felt embarrassed when no one joined in, and stopped." </strong>
</em></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18069269653551614796">This is reminded me of just how great Terry Pratchett is. His writing and humour is just fabulous and his characters are brilliant. However the plot of this novel is quite reminiscent of a wet tea towel. It doesn't hold a flame to <em>The Colour of Magic</em> and I'm quite glad that Pratchett gave up on the idea of doing sequels after this novel. It's overall very meh with a sprinkling of ugh. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer28491794">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11121456309003692816">Terry Prarchett is quickly becoming one of my favorite authors. Not only are the stories rich, funny, and enjoyable, but the format of the storytelling itself adds a whole separate dimension to the books. Pratchett clearly has an incredible understanding of, and love affair with, the English language, and that makes me not want to put these books down.<br /><br />From spending two pages arguing with the reader about why the female barbarian does not wear impractical sexy barbarian clothes, to subtle word ga</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11121456309003692816">Terry Prarchett is quickly becoming one of my favorite authors. Not only are the stories rich, funny, and enjoyable, but the format of the storytelling itself adds a whole separate dimension to the books. Pratchett clearly has an incredible understanding of, and love affair with, the English language, and that makes me not want to put these books down.<br /><br />From spending two pages arguing with the reader about why the female barbarian does not wear impractical sexy barbarian clothes, to subtle word games that not only work in the story but, when caught, made me laugh out loud, the entire book was incredible.<br /><br />Here are some of the many little gems hidden in there:	<br /><br />“Necrotelecomnicon,” said the dwarf. “Wizards use it. It’s how you contact the dead, I think.<br /><br />“… there was a whole bunch of people across the street helping themselves to musical instruments, can you believe that?”<br />“Yeah,” said Rincewind. “Luters, I expect.”<br /><br />“… while grinning like a necrophiliac in a morgue.”<br /><br />Just awesome.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_451419751">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451419751" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1188122-ben-babcock" class="left imgcol" title="Ben Babcock"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1211839871p2/1188122.jpg" alt="Ben Babcock" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/451419751?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1188122-ben-babcock" class="user" title="Ben Babcock">Ben Babcock</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/833445.The_Light_Fantastic" title="Paperback 9780552152594" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=humour" class="actionLinkLite">humour</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=2012-read" class="actionLinkLite">2012-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer451419751">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8367712698748700163">It’s been a long time since I read <em>The Colour Magic</em>. I’ve read a few other <em>Discworld</em> novels but am now kind of trying to read them in order. Terry Pratchett is a writer whose sense of humour aligns exactly with the type of humourous fiction I want to read: dry and absurd. From <em>Discworld</em> to <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50062626"> <em>Good Omens</em> </a>, Pratchett always delivers, and <em>The Light Fantastic</em> is no exception.<br /><br />I read the first half of this book with a sense of dragging anticipation. I was waiting for the book to <em>begin</em>. It took me a whil</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8367712698748700163">It’s been a long time since I read <em>The Colour Magic</em>. I’ve read a few other <em>Discworld</em> novels but am now kind of trying to read them in order. Terry Pratchett is a writer whose sense of humour aligns exactly with the type of humourous fiction I want to read: dry and absurd. From <em>Discworld</em> to <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50062626">
  <em>Good Omens</em>
</a>, Pratchett always delivers, and <em>The Light Fantastic</em> is no exception.<br /><br />I read the first half of this book with a sense of dragging anticipation. I was waiting for the book to <em>begin</em>. It took me a while to realize what <em>The Light Fantastic</em> reminds me of and, in so doing, allow me to change my mindset and enjoy it more. This book is very much like <em>The Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy</em>. There is a core group of characters—Rincewind, Twoflower, Cohen, Bethan, and of course, the Luggage—with occasional scenes featuring the antagonist or supporting cast. And this core group doesn’t so much <em>do</em> things as react to the various things that happen to them. Much like how Arthur Dent goes from lying in front of a bulldozer in his housecoat to tromping about the galaxy in a ship powered by an infinite improbability drive, Rincewind isn’t so much following a plan as trying to cope with the latest set of unfortunate circumstances in which he finds himself.<br /><br />Once I came to terms with this, <em>The Light Fantastic</em> became a lot more fun. I mean, that’s the point of <em>Discworld</em>: everything is just totally bonkers, from the elephants perched on the turtle’s back to the immense forces of magic. I think the word “romp” might have been invented solely to describe <em>Discworld</em> adventures.<br /><br />If I had to express any kind of disappointment about this book, it would simply be that there isn’t enough of it. It’s a slim volume. And there were segments where I wished Pratchett had delved more deeply into what was happening. For example, Death is present in this book, but in a more tangential capacity. Rincewind and Twoflower pay a visit to his hall but don’t stay very long, quickly showing themselves out. That’s understandable—I wouldn’t overstay my welcome at Death’s place either. But <em>The Light Fantastic</em> is very much a road comedy, and while that gives Pratchett plenty of opportunities for funny sequences, it also makes some of those sequences very fast, drive-by affairs.<br /><br />The calculus here is rather simple. Reading <em>Discworld</em>? Read it. If you haven’t read any <em>Discworld</em> novel, I probably wouldn’t start with this one. It’s a loose sequel to <em>The Colour Magic</em>, which I think was probably a stronger book (not that I remember all that much about it). So I would start there—or with another book later in the series, since this is one of those things where order doesn’t necessarily matter (combinations, not permutations!).<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/3.0/">
  <img width="88" height="31" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238653i/681550.png" alt="Creative Commons BY-NC License" /></a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8367712698748700163">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/247897978?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1669785-alex-ristea" class="user" title="Alex Ristea">Alex Ristea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/601239.The_Light_Fantastic" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552128483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=library" class="actionLinkLite">library</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=mmpb" class="actionLinkLite">mmpb</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer247897978">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5241955639046334685">It's a bit sad that I own the first 21 Discworld books and waited until Sir Terry Pratchett's passing to give them the attention they deserve.<br /><br />This is a wonderful book told in a distinctly British manner. It's not really a story with plot or characters, but likeable all the same.<br /><br />There are laughs and puns on every page, and it's a fun romp that shows the promise of this author and this series.<br /><br />Highly recommended that you start reading Discworld. I'm a nut for always going in published order, but I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5241955639046334685">It's a bit sad that I own the first 21 Discworld books and waited until Sir Terry Pratchett's passing to give them the attention they deserve.<br /><br />This is a wonderful book told in a distinctly British manner. It's not really a story with plot or characters, but likeable all the same.<br /><br />There are laughs and puns on every page, and it's a fun romp that shows the promise of this author and this series.<br /><br />Highly recommended that you start reading Discworld. I'm a nut for always going in published order, but I hear the best books are yet to come, so feel free to jump in somewhere later if you're put off by the first.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1233673009">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5163371357904044900"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/">More reviews at The BiblioSanctum</a>.<br /><br /><em>Darkness isn’t the opposite of light, it is simply its absence, and what was radiating from the book was the light that lies on the far side of darkness, the light fantastic.</em><br /><br />The Light Fantastic follows Rincewind and Twoflower after a strange, even stranger than normal, turn of events in The Color of Magic. Rincewind has gone from just being a bumbling tour guide for Twoflower to being the man that might actually have to save the world with Twoflower and Luggage</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5163371357904044900"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/">More reviews at The BiblioSanctum</a>.<br /><br /><em>Darkness isn’t the opposite of light, it is simply its absence, and what was radiating from the book was the light that lies on the far side of darkness, the light fantastic.</em><br /><br />The Light Fantastic follows Rincewind and Twoflower after a strange, even stranger than normal, turn of events in The Color of Magic. Rincewind has gone from just being a bumbling tour guide for Twoflower to being the man that might actually have to save the world with Twoflower and Luggage as part of his heroic entourage, which Rincewind is very skeptical about and feels like hiding is probably the better solution to the problem.<br /><br />The Light Fantastic found its footing immediately being both engaging and funny from its opening lines:<br /><br /><blockquote>The sun rose slowly, as if it wasn’t sure it was worth all the effort.</blockquote><br /><br />I’m not sure how much time passed between the publishing of these two books, but to me, this book was much better paced than the first book. It seemed to be a more confident endeavor as Pratchett’s writing pushed past being cautiously humorous to pretty laugh-out-loud funny. It’s the kind of book that made me smile throughout the day when I think about the antics and Pratchett’s clever use of word play. As I mentioned, I was a little worried that the rest of the books might continue to be like the first. Don’t get me wrong, though. The first book isn’t bad, but mind would often wander when the writing stopped engaging me with the first book. I didn’t have that problem with this book.<br /><br />I liked Rincewind much better in this book, too. I felt the character really got a chance to flourish in this story. There were more facets of his personality presented here and it was interesting to watch him grow as a character during this adventure.<br /><br />Nigel Planer’s narration of these books was lively. He’s an excellent voice for this series. The only complaint I have (and it’s not with the narrator) is that the quality of these audiobooks aren’t the greatest. I guess they just took the old recordings (maybe) and made them digital. The narration quality for The Light Fantastic is much better than the narration quality for The Color of Magic. It was a bit muddled sounding, but Planer is such a great narrator that I’ll continue to listen to these books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5163371357904044900">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11494541402773899242">Sabes cuando saboreas las palabras, pero también las engulles y a la vez te sientes culpable de estar devorándolas demasiado rápido? Pues eso me ha pasado con esta segunda entrega de Mundodisco. No hay una sola frase que esté de más y todas están trabajadísimas, como si Pratchett hubiese estado puliéndolas durante días.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText11494541402773899242">Sabes cuando saboreas las palabras, pero también las engulles y a la vez te sientes culpable de estar devorándolas demasiado rápido? Pues eso me ha pasado con esta segunda entrega de Mundodisco. No hay una sola frase que esté de más y todas están trabajadísimas, como si Pratchett hubiese estado puliéndolas durante días. Sabes que lo que estás leyendo es la mejor versión posible. Y te ríes mucho, que esa es la otra. Pratchett tiene un humor muy absurdo que encaja muy bien con el estilo de humor que más me gusta. En resumen, un entretenimiento excelente.<br /><br />Al menos hasta las últimas veinte páginas. Es entonces cuando Pratchett se da cuenta que tiene que resolver la trama y lo hace deprisa y corriendo y sin ningún tipo de originalidad. Incluso el humor se resiente. Pero es un pequeño "pero" para tan divertida novela.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39419822">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer150397788327560662">Open confession for the first half of this book I was asking myself why I was reading, to which I could only respond I liked the other one. A lot of this book feels extremely shallow. Not I'm so pretty and my hair smells terrific shallow of course. I believe that a book should somehow challenge and expand you. I didn't clearly get that from the first chunk of this book. That is what I mean by shallow. <br /><br />The last half of the book once things start happening is very entertaining. I have to say that</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText150397788327560662">Open confession for the first half of this book I was asking myself why I was reading, to which I could only respond I liked the other one. A lot of this book feels extremely shallow. Not I'm so pretty and my hair smells terrific shallow of course. I believe that a book should somehow challenge and expand you. I didn't clearly get that from the first chunk of this book. That is what I mean by shallow. <br /><br />The last half of the book once things start happening is very entertaining. I have to say that Pratchett is not giving Adams a run for his money. But they are books that you can write two papers and skim three books on pragmatism and still read a chunk of. While I love Cioran and Le Brun they just are not going to reach their full potential when they are running on empty. Pratchett on the other hand feels like he is at least coming close. <br /><br />Plus I like that the main character is a coward, completely inept, and still almost dies at least once every 20 pages (the count was 27 around the center of the book according to his sidekick, who appears to have glasses not 4 eyes). <br /><br />There was discontinuity again but I'm starting to think Terry just wasn't prepared for a reader who was going to remember his characters vocabularies and call him on the fact they are claiming to not know the meaning of words that they previously used. <br /><br />There is a fun satire of religion that comes off as an extremely watered down version of the mist by Stephen King. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17237398196072796980">I'm a latecomer to the <em>Discworld,</em> having just discovered it a couple of years ago. Whenever I need a good laugh-out-loud escapist novel, I know Sir Terry can deliver. I started with the Tiffany Aching series*, and have managed to read 7-8 of the little <em>Discworld</em> suckers** so far, and enjoyed every one of them immensely, including this one.***<br /><br />*Actually, and just so I don't bring the wrath of the ghost of Olaf Quimby II down on me, I discovered Pratchett via <em>Good Omens</em> many years ago, but at the t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17237398196072796980">I'm a latecomer to the <em>Discworld,</em> having just discovered it a couple of years ago. Whenever I need a good laugh-out-loud escapist novel, I know Sir Terry can deliver. I started with the Tiffany Aching series*, and have managed to read 7-8 of the little <em>Discworld</em> suckers** so far, and enjoyed every one of them immensely, including this one.***<br /><br />*Actually, and just so I don't bring the wrath of the ghost of Olaf Quimby II down on me, I discovered Pratchett via <em>Good Omens</em> many years ago, but at the time ascribed the writing style to Mr. Gaiman, which was good because I then went on to devour everything Gaiman ever wrote****, including <em>Sandman</em>*****, which was a major find, but didn't pick up a <em>Discworld</em> novel****** until a number of years later when a friend badgered me into reading <em>Wee Free Men</em>, which was delightful. <br /><br />**not to say that they suck, although perhaps some of the creatures contained within could be accused of sucking, but only as a function of how they kill... or eat... or, um... suck...<br /><br />*** “immense” being measured partially by how often I'm compelled to read sections aloud to my longsuffering******* husband, then waiting for him to laugh.<br /><br />****well, not technically, since I am sure there are many things he has written, which I haven't discovered yet.<br /><br />*****and to be specific, I mean that I've read almost all of <em>Sandman</em>, but have yet to complete the <em>Absolute Vol. 4</em>********, mainly because it's so freaking heavy I have to sit in my special chair to read it, and my special chair is currently being used as a prop for photographing dogs, and it's very difficult to read by strobe. <br /><br />******although technically, I suppose one would put <em>Good Omens</em> in the <em>Discworld</em>... er... world, so I guess one would say I HAD read a <em>Discworld</em> novel before <em>Wee Free Men</em>.<br /><br />*******He is either “longsuffering,” or else he has gotten very good at listening for me to take a breath, then responding with “hmmm,” or “hahaha,” whichever is most appropriate. <br /><br />********I also have yet to read <em>Absolute Death</em>*********, not because it's so heavy, (it is considerably lighter,) but because I haven't yet purchased it.<br /><br />*********I have, however, read <em>Death: The High Cost of Living</em>, although not <em>Death: The Time of Your Life</em>. I have also read <em>Black Orchid</em>, but that's not really a <em>Sandman</em> story**********, so I'm not sure how it's relevant here. <br /><br />**********And, since this DID start out as a <em>Discworld</em> review, I'm afraid that not much of this is relevant, except in the way that they are all books. That I have read. Mostly.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_9529476">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9529476" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/175268-bonnie" class="left imgcol" title="Bonnie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1249874214p2/175268.jpg" alt="Bonnie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/9529476?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/175268-bonnie" class="user" title="Bonnie">Bonnie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=fantasy-sf" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-sf</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=library-books" class="actionLinkLite">library-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/175268-bonnie?shelf=series-in-progress" class="actionLinkLite">series-in-progress</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9529476">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14511932378570839444">This is the second Discworld book, and I found it just as funny as the first, with perhaps a more straightforward plot, which I appreciated. It's very much a continuation of the first book, so I would recommend reading that one before this. <br /><br />Rincewind is back again, and the spell trapped in his head is the only thing that can keep the world from coming to a flaming explosive end at the hands of a giant red hot comet that is getting closer and closer to the Discworld. <br /><br />The wizards who know about th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14511932378570839444">This is the second Discworld book, and I found it just as funny as the first, with perhaps a more straightforward plot, which I appreciated. It's very much a continuation of the first book, so I would recommend reading that one before this. <br /><br />Rincewind is back again, and the spell trapped in his head is the only thing that can keep the world from coming to a flaming explosive end at the hands of a giant red hot comet that is getting closer and closer to the Discworld. <br /><br />The wizards who know about this have set out to find him, but the only problem is that Rincewind cannot be found....well, there may be one more problem, and that's the fact that Rincewind is remarkably good at getting himself into near death experiences--with the help of Twoflower, the naive and careless tourist he is tourguiding--and who knows what will happen to the Discworld if Rincewind should actually die with the spell still trapped in his head? This might be the end of Discworld, given the fact that Rincewind and Twoflower have already fallen off the edge of Discworld at the start of the book!<br /><br />Hilarity ensues. It's a rare book that is adventuresome and funny at the same time, and Terry Pratchett is fantastic at it. <br />I have to say my favorite part is when Rincewind is questioning how he's been able to keep this powerful spell in his brain without going crazy, and then rethinks if he in fact IS crazy, and then decides that he is not, because even when the trees talked to him (and they did about 100 pages earlier) he didn't talk back. It's unusually great because Pratchett remembered that earlier situation, and so, also, does the reader, so the reader is almost in on an inside joke between the author, character, and reader. That takes talent!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14511932378570839444">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
