<span id="freeTextContainer17083640613837241693">Discworld is probably the only fantasy series I'd recommend not reading in chronological order - rather, read by character in chronological order. Wik</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17083640613837241693">Discworld is probably the only fantasy series I'd recommend not reading in chronological order - rather, read by character in chronological order. Wikipedia has a nice little chart: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discworld" target="_blank">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discworld</a><br /><br />The Death ones remain my over-all favorites, although the Witches are a close second. Favorite Discworld books that are must-reads: <a title="Small Gods" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Small%20Gods">Small Gods</a>, <a title="The Truth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=The%20Truth">The Truth</a>, and <a title="Thief of Time" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Thief%20of%20Time">Thief of Time</a>.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/1176067-jackie?shelf=nook-books" class="actionLinkLite">nook-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer837386650">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7371063674940572488">I was told by several readers that this series improves as it hits its stride and I can definitely see that is true. One of my complaints about The Color of Magic was that I found the many digressions and footnotes distracting. While, The Light Fantastic has some digressions and footnotes there were certainly less of them. Also, because most of the worldbuilding occurred in the first book there was much less info-dumping. This made the book much more reader friendly. <br /><br />What I loved about The Light</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7371063674940572488">I was told by several readers that this series improves as it hits its stride and I can definitely see that is true. One of my complaints about The Color of Magic was that I found the many digressions and footnotes distracting. While, The Light Fantastic has some digressions and footnotes there were certainly less of them. Also, because most of the worldbuilding occurred in the first book there was much less info-dumping. This made the book much more reader friendly. <br /><br />What I loved about The Light Fantastic were the literary references. Cohen the Barbarian was absolutely hysterical. I found myself having to check myself while reading in public so I wouldn’t look like a crazy person. You know how non-readers just don’t get it. Anyway, I can now see the appeal of this series and I look forward to reading the next one. <br /></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/2492588-katie" class="user" title="Katie">Katie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2492588-katie?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2492588-katie?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2492588-katie?shelf=comedy" class="actionLinkLite">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1456437086">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2756140670425355024">I've read three Discworld novels by now, and it's hard for me to imagine ever really giving one less than three stars (barring an unexpected and drastic drop in quality). I just find Pratchett's style to be so charming and fun that even a mediocre plot is going to be something that I really enjoy reading. <br /><br />I thought that <em>The Light Fantastic</em> was a step up from <em>The Color of Magic</em>, if only because the plot is much tighter and more coherent (the episodic nature of the latter really just wasn't my cup</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2756140670425355024">I've read three Discworld novels by now, and it's hard for me to imagine ever really giving one less than three stars (barring an unexpected and drastic drop in quality). I just find Pratchett's style to be so charming and fun that even a mediocre plot is going to be something that I really enjoy reading. <br /><br />I thought that <em>The Light Fantastic</em> was a step up from <em>The Color of Magic</em>, if only because the plot is much tighter and more coherent (the episodic nature of the latter really just wasn't my cup of tea). <br /><br />I'm curious to see how Pratchett's books compare to each other: given the three I've read, he seems very found of pairing a deeply naive guy with a largely-cynical-but-good-at-heart guy, and then face them off against a wizard or a bureaucrat (or, here, a wizard-bureaucrat) who clearly wants too much power. This is a pretty solid setup for Pratchett's style, and the sameness of it doesn't bother me yet, but I'm curious to see how much he does (or does not) deviate from the formula.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2756140670425355024">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><img alt="1654" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p2/1654.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7225036720166814886">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7225036720166814886">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <em>The Color of Magic</em>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <em>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</em>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <em>Good Omens</em>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <em>Nation</em>. Terry published <em>Snuff</em> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7225036720166814886">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Terry Pratchett...</a>
